# Build with AI: Beyond Pair Programming with AI

> Effective use of AI coding assistants can speed up and improve the software development process through rapid code generation, iteration, experimentation, and a modern take on test-driven development (TDD). Apply AI tools to build and expand coding projects, create new components by generating fit-for-purpose boilerplate code, validate projects with AI-generated tests, automatically document and e

### Introduction

#### Pair-programming with AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/pair-programming-with-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/pair-programming-with-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - AI tools used carefully and with skill can significantly improve the way you work and the work you produce as a programmer.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/pair-programming-with-ai?u=76281980&t=7)** And in this course we'll focus on those crucial works carefully and with skill.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/pair-programming-with-ai?u=76281980&t=13)** You see, programming isn't just about writing code, it's about understanding what the code is supposed to do, what problem or task or goal it's meant to solve, and then how best to design and build code-based system to solve them so we can invest more of our time and uniquely human skills and knowledge and understanding on building the best applications and products possible.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/pair-programming-with-ai?u=76281980&t=35)** AI powered coding tools are the latest step in a long evolutionary chain of specialized developer tools that check our work and automate our processes and supercharge our human skills, and I'm here to help you use them with care and skill and get it right.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/pair-programming-with-ai?u=76281980&t=50)** Let's get cracking.

#### Prerequisites and how to use the exercise files

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] This is not a project course, and while I strongly encourage you to play along and test out the different tools and techniques covered, it's also not a hands-on coding course.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=9)** It's more of a, here's how I think you can do things with AI coding tools, and I invite you to try these techniques to see if they work for you, type course.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=18)** Now, throughout the course, I'll be demoing GitHub Copilot, ChatGPT, Cursor, and Claude.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=24)** And if you want to follow along in every demo, you need accounts for all these services.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=29)** That is not a prerequisite, though.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=31)** And these are also not the only AI coding tools available, so don't feel pressure to get or use any one of them.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=38)** This course is about a mindset as much as it is about practical application, and you can watch it without using any AI tool.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=45)** So play along, or sit back and watch, or do a combination.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=50)** You know what you came here for and how best to reach your goal.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=54)** I say all this because, on first blush, the GitHub repository with exercise files for this course may appear a bit of a mishmash of unfinished and disconnected pieces, because it is.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=66)** What I've provided here are samples you can use if you want to, and ignore if you don't, that allow you to play along with me and then play around yourself later, without having to do a huge amount of setup.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=79)** A fair portion of the demos I go through in this course will use GitHub Copilot in GitHub Codespaces, and that's what this exercise file repo is mostly for.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=88)** So when you see me in this environment, you can spin up your own Codespace and jump right in to replicate what I'm doing, and I encourage you to do so, because what you'll find is something extraordinary that is central to the purpose of this course.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=104)** If you do exactly what I do, type in the exact same code or prompts, or click on the same buttons in the same sequence, there's a good chance you'll get a different result from mine.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=115)** Realizing this and making it an expectation as you work with AI coding tools is essential to your success.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=123)** Right now, all AI coding tools are implementations of large language models, and these models are probabilistic and non-deterministic.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=132)** That means the same request can and will produce different results, because most coding problems have multiple different solutions.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=139)** So to get the most out of this course, go check out the GitHub repository and play along with me when you see me doing demos.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/prerequisites-and-how-to-use-the-exercise-files?u=76281980&t=147)** Or not, it's entirely up to you.

### 1. Tools, Materials, and Environments

#### Tools, materials, and environments
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=0)** - Here's a radical idea.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=2)** What if we accidentally hacked ourselves when we built a class of software tools that appear to understand and use our language?
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=10)** You see, our brains are hardwired to perceive language as meaningful communication.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=15)** So when something produces something that appears to us as language, be it a talking parrot or a large language model, we can't help but think there is meaning in the words and sentences produced.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=28)** And that a thinking entity, not unlike ourselves, produce them.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=32)** And when we start thinking of a language machine as a thinking entity like ourselves, we start treating it accordingly.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=39)** Attributing motivations and behaviors and expectations to it the way we would to a human collaborator.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=46)** Getting frustrated when communication seems to break down and getting worried the machine might take our jobs.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=53)** This is a problem and I have a simple fix that works for me and probably will work for you too.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=60)** When I think and talk about AI coding tools, I call them that.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=64)** Tools.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=65)** Because that's what they are.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=67)** Tools in the same way that syntax highlighting and autocomplete, and linters, and formatters, and test suites are tools.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=75)** Don't get me wrong here.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=76)** They are enormously powerful tools.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=79)** They sometimes function in fundamentally different ways from all our other tools.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=84)** And we interact and use them in new ways, but they are still very much tools and should be treated as such.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=91)** Additionally, and unlike any other tool we've had before, they can also serve as materials we can use to build new tools.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=99)** Think using an AI system to create a new custom coding assistant.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=103)** And you start getting the idea.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=105)** And lastly, AI coding tools can serve as environments, currently exemplified by Claude Artifacts, where the AI not only generates code, but spins it up and runs it as a throwaway app.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=118)** And this is a bleeding edge capability we're still trying to make sense of.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=122)** And it opens up new and unexplored opportunities and possibility space for how we build, interact with, and use software.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=131)** So as we get started, get used to this framing.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=135)** AI coding tools are tools.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=138)** Those tools can be used as materials and can produce their own environments.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=143)** That is all they are.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/tools-materials-and-environments?u=76281980&t=145)** And this is how we approach them, as tools.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Definitions:** is a  (2)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Code Keywords:** function (1)
> **Speakers:** - here (1)

#### AI as a chatty collaborator
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=0)** - When ChatGPT was first introduced to the world in November 2022, someone asked me how a language model could be so good at writing code?
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=8)** It's a great question, though I don't think the person asking was particularly satisfied with my answer, so you be the judge.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=15)** Here's my answer.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=16)** Language models are good at writing code because code is just language and unlike the messy contextual natural language we humans use to communicate, coding languages are pedantically logical and structured and templated and conforming and rigid, and this makes them easy to model and easy to reproduce.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=35)** The reason coding proficiency of LLMs is so confounding to us is, at least in my mind, that these software systems are amorphous blobs of hypothetical capabilities.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=46)** They don't come with a list of possible uses.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=49)** Instead, we throw prompts at them and see what comes out.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=52)** And more often than not, if we throw a sentence about code or even code on its own, what comes out is correct code that we can paste into an application and run without further modification, which is profoundly weird to us because that's not at all how we ourselves work and also a strong reminder that these tools are nothing like us.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=75)** As I said before, the reason we can't shake the feeling they are like us is because they also output things that look to us like our language.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=84)** And this is where things get really interesting, because language models can produce both natural language and code, we can prompt them with instructions, code, and a mix of both, and in return, they output completions containing natural language, code, or a mix of both.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=104)** This can be useful and can also be really frustrating.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=108)** In particular, when you use tools like ChatGPT that are configured to be chatty, and this is why specialized coding tools like GitHub Copilot and Cursor exist, to separate concerns between the chatty natural language part and the code-producing part.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=126)** That doesn't mean you can't get ChatGPT and its class of tools to do the same though, quite the contrary.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=132)** When we approach chatty AI systems for what they are, spicy auto-complete machines, we can get them to produce the completions we need in the way we need them to.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=143)** Let me show you the two main approaches that work for me.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=146)** First, basic prompting.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=148)** If you give ChatGPT task like, "Write a react component to display a product card with an image, title, product rating, description, price, and add to cart button," the completion will start with some chatty natural language like, "Certainly, here is a ReactJS component to blah, blah, blah, blah, blah," followed by the code snippet, some more language, then maybe another code snippet and a full explanation at the end.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=173)** If you're new to React or learning a new technique, this is useful.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=177)** If you were just looking for the code, it's a lot of extra noise.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=181)** To get rid of that noise, treat the tool like a tool by configuring it to give you what you want.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=187)** "Write a React component to display a product card with an image, title, product rating, description, price, and add to card button.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=194)** Only the code. No explanation."
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=197)** And just like that, ChatGPT gives you a nice clean code block with no extra noise.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=202)** The second approach is a bit different and also a lot more volatile.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=207)** If you prompt a language model in English, the completions are in English.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=211)** If you then prompt it in Norwegian, the completion is in Norwegian because it's a spicy auto complete machine.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=218)** From this follows an interesting phenomenon.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=220)** If you prompt a language model in code, it tends to respond in code.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=225)** Now I said this is volatile, and here's why.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=227)** ChatGPT and similar chat tools have been configured to try to run code when they can.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=232)** So if you prompt them with code, they may try to run it and it's difficult to know and control when that happens.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=239)** In other words, this technique is less helpful if you're trying to get the system to write code, but can be helpful if you're trying to get the system to do something with that code.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=249)** For example, if you input a JSON object providing instructions on how you want the system to behave, the spicy auto complete will likely complete the correct output as if the instructions in the JSON object were followed.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-as-a-chatty-collaborator?u=76281980&t=264)** This has some really interesting applications and opens the door to a lot of experimentation that falls way outside the scope of this course, and it can also be super helpful as you work through complex challenges, so we'll check it out.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** throw (2), return, (1), let (1), super (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (2), in other words (1)
> **Env Vars:** json (2)
> **Analogies:** just like (1), for example (1)
> **Tools:** github (1)

#### AI in the IDE
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=0)** - The place developers encounter and use AI tools the most is in their preferred IDE, and we can expect this integration to become deeper and more normalized as the developer community figures out what AI interactions work best and where they fit most naturally into the workflow.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=16)** We're already seeing clear signs of this with how AI tools work in our IDEs today.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=22)** Extensions like GitHub Copilot add a wide range of deep integrations into existing IDEs and new IDEs like Cursor and Replit are built around AI tools to make them a natural part of the workflow.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=36)** AI interactions in the IDE can take many forms.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=39)** At the code level, AI tools can work as supercharged code completion, not just finishing a variable name or a function declaration or providing a boiler plate or scaffolding, but proposing entire blocks of code with your variables and other elements already wired in and allowing you to iterate through different variations and proposals.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=60)** Inline chat enables you to prompt the AI tool describing what you want to achieve, and the system uses the current file or even all the files in the project as reference as it builds out a proposed solution you can then accept or modify or reject.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=76)** Bring up a separate chat panel, and you can discuss your code with the AI system, asking it to explain what a highlighted section of code does, refactor all or part of a file, and test, add new features, or even build out entire projects.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-ide?u=76281980&t=92)** AI integrated into your IDE gives you an always on, always available coding collaborator tool that can transform, expand, refactor, document, test, and generate new code in moments so you spend less time writing code and get more time to review the work and make sure it's working correctly.

>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-pilot-seat?u=76281980&t=103)** And if you try to get them to build anything more complex, things start going off the rails almost immediately, which is why some developers say AI coding tools are useless.

>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-pilot-seat?u=76281980&t=131)** The new AI powered Chat2 software path makes the ability to create custom throwaway software available to everyone, meaning those superpowers developers have had to quickly spin up a script to do some data cleaning or collect a bunch of info from a source or automate a repetitive task is becoming available to everyone, and I expect we'll see this space continue to expand, both in capabilities and usage, for a long time.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-pilot-seat?u=76281980&t=159)** At the same time, the inability of AI tools to build advanced applications, especially ones that involve complex user interactions and flows, or perform intricate data operations across large domains, not only highlights, but emphasizes the need for real human developers in the mix.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-pilot-seat?u=76281980&t=178)** In the end, most software is created to serve a human purpose, and only a human has the ability to understand when that purpose is served and the software is successful.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-in-the-pilot-seat?u=76281980&t=189)** So while AI can be in the pilot seat for basic projects and drastically reduced the time to boot up fully functional prototypes and baseline applications, the moment the need goes beyond the very basic tasks you could solve in a few hours by pulling together templates and other tools, AI tools very much return to their natural state as tools wielded by skilled craftspeople for optimal results.

>

>

>

>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=113)** When cars arrived and owners needed assistance maintaining them because of the dirt roads, they naturally turned to the mechanics because they were the ones that were fixing the horses and buggies, and some of those mechanics specialized in maintaining this new form of transportation technology.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=131)** Why am I talking about mechanics and horses and cars?
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=134)** Because software developers have experienced similar transitions at a dramatically accelerated rate for the entire time we've had software to develop.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=143)** As hardware and infrastructure evolved from giant room-sized computers running off punch cards and tape reels, to tiny pocket-sized computers, permanently tethered to the mobile internet, so did every aspect of our work.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=159)** In fact, the only things that have not changed much since the information age began is our input and output surfaces.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=167)** We still primarily use keyboards for input and screens for output.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=172)** Artificial Intelligence both grew out of this evolution of information technology and is the natural progression of the tools we use to build information technology.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=183)** And developers are already primed for this latest evolution because we built every stepping stone that brought us here and changed and expanded our skills with every step.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=196)** Our language shapes our understanding of the world and our role in it, and the language we choose to use When we talk about tools like AI influences what agency and capabilities we think we have and what role we believe we get to play in building our own future.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=213)** So here, let me give you the language I choose when I talk about developers and how their work is impacted by AI.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=222)** AI tools give every developer new capabilities that in turn give them more agency.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=229)** With AI tools, we can leave more of the rote coding work to finely tuned computers, so we developers have more time and cognitive space to use our human insight and ingenuity to build better software.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=244)** If you think critically about it, a lot of development work is being a human input device to a computer system to do things like, string different tools together, or format data and code to match, or apply standard components or templates and do endless repetitive tasks.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=263)** With AI, much of that input and stringing together and formatting and templating and repetition can be offloaded to a machine that can do it faster and more efficiently so we can focus on what comes next, or what the code we're building is actually for, or how to make it better.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=282)** To me, the new role of AI power developer is to take a step up from being an expert code writer to becoming a knowledgeable overseer of the totality of the work.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=294)** With these new tools, we become responsible for what the code does instead of how the code is written.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=301)** And over time, that role will transform into something new and completely different.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=306)** So, like the blacksmiths evolving into car mechanics, those of us who choose to embrace AI coding tools will rapidly transition into new types of work with new unique challenges and opportunities.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=319)** And like modern day blacksmiths, those who choose to stay with the craft of handwritten code will find value and work and societal novelty in this soon to become very different way of doing things.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=332)** And just to release that extra bit of tension I know I just created, this transition is not immediate and will take a long time to work itself out.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=342)** For now, and for the immediate future, my advice to you is this, accept the reality that the work and purpose of a developer is always in flux, and the true craft of our work is our ability to go where that flux takes us next.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=358)** So, as you step into this new paradigm of AI power development, embrace an always learning mindset and push hard into these new technologies to not just use them, but find out where they are actually useful, and lead your peers and the industry in those directions.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=378)** We have an opportunity here to shape the future of development for developers.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=383)** Nothing is decided, no future is inevitable.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=387)** We have the right and the power and the duty to build this future for ourselves and those who come after us.
>
> **[6:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-rethinking-what-a-developer-is?u=76281980&t=395)** So, in the next chapters, we'll start that work by finding out what these AI tools can do and where we can do better work using them.

### 2. Looking the AI in the Mouth

#### Where to start and how to start
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=0)** - If you're new to working with AI coding tools, you're justified in wondering where to start and how to start.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=5)** There are so many different tools out there and whomever you ask, they'll tell you their favorite tool and prompt technique and magical alchemic AI incantation is the thing that will thousand X your developer skills.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=21)** And don't forget to like and subscribe.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=24)** So let me peel away all the marketing layers and all the nonsense and get all the way down to the core.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=32)** First, as with most things, the best place to start is where you're already comfortable.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=37)** As a developer, that's probably in your current IDE.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=41)** And the best tool to start with is therefore whatever is the most integrated tool you can find for that IDE.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=48)** I use VS Code and GitHub Codespaces and if you do the same, I'd say the most logical tool to start with is GitHub Copilot.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=55)** If you're using a different IDE with its own preferred AI extension, pick that one.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=60)** The key here is to find the AI extension that fits most naturally into the existing environment and workflow.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=66)** And that will differ depending on where you are, what tools you're using, what you're building, and what services you rely on to build it.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=74)** If you're not ready for or comfortable with or able to use integrated coding tools, maybe your workplace has been blocked or they're not available in your region, or the cost is too high at the moment, standalone AI chat apps like ChatGPT and Claude provide robust coding support as well.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=92)** And these supports are rapidly expanding and becoming more useful.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=97)** These tools serve as good secondary entry points to the world of AI coding and are also great places for isolated experimentation, more complex chats, and long chains of iteration over a theme.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=110)** I have access to and subscribed to a long list of tools, both internal, integrated, and standalone.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=117)** And I used them all in combination.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=119)** So I can tell you from lived experience, there is no single right answer to how you want to proceed here.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=126)** Whatever feels right for you is what's right for you.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=130)** So in this chapter, I'll walk you through the basics of using both integrated and standalone AI tools to augment your coding work.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=139)** I invite you to play along in whatever tools you have available and prefer.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=144)** And as I do so, I want you to remember two important things.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=149)** First, most of what you see me do in one tool can be done in any of the other tools in the same category.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=157)** So generating inline AI completions with GitHub Copilot works the same way as generating inline code completions with Cursor and so on.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=166)** And second, even if you follow me exactly, using the same code and the same prompts, chances are you'll get a different completion.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=174)** This is the nature of AI coding tools and is not an error.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/where-to-start-and-how-to-start?u=76281980&t=178)** Embrace this non-determinism and learn to use it to your advantage.

#### Generating documentation

#### Documentation-Driven Development (DDD?)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=0)** - You've heard of test driven development.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=2)** Now get ready for documentation driven development.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=6)** One unique thing about being a programmer is the code we write and the environments we work in are constantly evolving and changing.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=14)** To stay current and write the best code for right now means we have to constantly update our knowledge and rethink our strategies and change our best practices.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=23)** And this process of constantly learning and adapting is something we humans are really well equipped to do, even though it can be really difficult and time consuming, and it's also something AI coding assistance can't do at all.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=39)** I'll talk more about this later on, but the basic premise is this.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=43)** Language models can only reproduce language patterns from their training data.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=48)** They can't learn anything new.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=51)** To add new patterns to a language model, you have to either rebuild it from scratch or create a fine tuned or distilled model.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=59)** Language models also tend to reproduce what's most prevalent in its patterns, which, in code, means old ways of doing things.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=68)** In other words, when you use AI coding tools, part of your job as a human coder is to ensure that AI uses the latest coding standards and practices.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=79)** The good news is language models are bias amplification machines, and when you prompt a language model, you're actually biasing it towards whatever is in your prompt.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=91)** That means if you need the AI coding tool to use a new coding strategy or module or something else it doesn't do on its own, you can do so by providing it with documentation and examples of what you want.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=105)** As I've explained before, coding languages are highly structured and patterned, and language models are designed to reproduce language structures and patterns.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=113)** So biasing the system by giving it documentation and examples usually causes the system to reproduce these new patterns.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=122)** Here's one example of how to do this.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=124)** In this React and TypeScript project, the AI coding tool keeps insisting on using explicit function components with the shorthand React.fc, even though this isn't a recommended pattern any longer.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=137)** To get the AI to change its default bias and apply a new pattern, I'll grab some documentation about how to write function components without React.fc, then prompt the AI to write the code to match this new pattern.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=152)** And it does.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=153)** And if I'm using an integrated AI tool like GitHub, Copilot, or Cursor, it'll recognize this pattern going forward and use it for future function declarations most of the time.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=166)** My recommended best practice for you is to always stay on top of the latest standards and practices for whatever code language and application you're using, and monitor what the AI coding tool does.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/documentation-driven-development-ddd?u=76281980&t=178)** Anytime it starts reproducing old patterns, grab the official documentation and a practical code example of how you want the code to be implemented, and then prompt AI to follow this pattern, and it'll mostly do that, which is why I call this documentation driven development.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** function (3), this. (2), new. (1), module (1)
> **Best Practices:** recommended (2), best practice (1)
> **Tools:** github (1)
> **Definitions:** in other words (1)
> **Speakers:** - you (1)

>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/chatting-with-code?u=76281980&t=8)** This is especially useful if you are inspecting code someone else has written or you're trying to maintain some larger thing where you need to pull in pieces from disparate parts and you're not fully aware of how they work together or what's actually going on.

#### Code from a chat (ChatGPT)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So far, I've been demonstrating how to use AI coding tools in context inside an IDE.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=5)** And this is the most natural entry point, but it's not the only entry point for this.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=10)** You can also use standalone AI chat tools like ChatGPT to perform the same types of tasks.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=17)** The main difference is you're no longer working inside an IDE so if you want any of this code to run, you need to copy and paste it into an IDE.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=25)** But there are advantages to using ChatGPT or another chat interface to generate code in that you can then isolate your conversation.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=33)** It's not in context, it's not going to mess with any of the other code, it's also not going to look at any of the other code, and it's a very nice confined space to work on code.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=43)** There are a couple of things you can do here.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=44)** So first we can just ask ChatGPT to generate some code for us.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=48)** I'll say create a react component using TSX, using TypeScript that has an input field for latitude and longitude and submits button
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=71)** and validates the values before submission, ask question.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=79)** Let's see what it does now.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=81)** Because we're no longer in the coding environment, instead of getting just a code, we get a conversation.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=87)** So the system is now explaining what it's doing.
>

>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=94)** Then it gives you the actual code you can see here.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=98)** And then at the bottom it explains what this component is and how it works.

>

>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=110)** So it can say, I want the user to input latitude and longitude in two different fields and validate each of them independently.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=131)** They need to have real values and the error message should reflect the error.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=144)** Now ChatGPT builds out a much more comprehensive component for me that has more pieces to it.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=150)** And if you look at this huge example here compared to what I have over here, you quickly see the results here are vastly different.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=161)** And this is the first thing I want to highlight.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=163)** Even though GitHub, Copilot and ChatGPT run off similar models, they behave quite differently and it's often useful to use them both in combination.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=172)** For example, if I'm building out a new component, I may go to ChatGPT to build out the core elements of the component and then bring them into VS Code and then continue working there with GitHub, Copilot, because I find this chat interface to be more welcoming and also allow me to do a lot more iteration than I can do inside GitHub, Copilot.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=195)** Also, if I go off the rails and the system isn't giving me what I want, I can just abandon it and it won't have any impact on the project as a whole.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=204)** But there's more.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=206)** In ChatGPT, there is now a brand new feature called canvas.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=210)** Here you can collaborate using code.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=213)** So let's start a new chat and ask for the same thing.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=239)** The canvas feature here pops my code out into a separate code editor.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=245)** So now I have the chat on the left and the code editor on the right.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=248)** And because of this layout, I can now have the same type of behavior in ChatGPT that I did in VS Code with GitHub, Copilot.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=257)** So now that the code is built, I can go down into this section down here and get a code review.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=262)** I can also port it to a different language.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=264)** I can fix bugs within the code, add logs to the code, and even add comments to the code.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=270)** So this gives me a lot of new capabilities and also a completely different interface to work with that is more closely aligned with how we work with the IDEs.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=278)** So you can see, working here and working here at the same time actually makes sense because these two interfaces are different, they give you different tools and they can work in combination by simply copying and pasting things back and forth.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/code-from-a-chat-chatgpt?u=76281980&t=292)** And yes, that does sound tedious, but from my experience, it's actually more effective than only working in one environment.

#### Knowledge, trust, and conservative models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=1)** - [Narrator] Okay, now that you have a firm understanding of how to work with AI coding tools, I want to ground you in some challenging truths as you get started.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=8)** Language models do not know anything, have no understanding of what you are doing, have no context or reference, and can't learn anything new.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=18)** They are models of language and they reproduce token sequences based on the prevalent patterns surfaced from the data they were built on.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=26)** I know these are controversial statements, especially in pro AI circles, and when you work with these models using natural language, it's easy to start thinking of them as thinking machines with real world understandings.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=38)** But when you work with them to do challenging things like coding, you quickly run up against these issues.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=46)** You see, here's the thing.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=46)** If you believe these tools to be intelligent and knowledgeable and they serve up old, incorrect and even broken code, it's easy to discard them as incompetent and more or less useless.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=59)** If, on the other hand you think of them as advanced spicy auto complete machines, you can tune by providing context, your interactions with them change.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=68)** There are three big things to remember when you work with AI coding tools.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=73)** First, they are not knowledge bases.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=76)** They don't look up any information in the database or documentation or online when they generate completions, they repeat prevalent patterns in the data they've been built from.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=86)** This means a model with a cutoff date of April 1st, 2023, has no ability to surface any patterns of things introduced after that date.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=97)** So if you need the AI coding tool to replicate new patterns, it has no previous exposure to, use the documentation driven development strategy I introduced earlier in the chapter.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=107)** This biases the system towards your new documentation and examples and gives it the ability to replicate those patterns.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=115)** And this brings us to the second point.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=117)** Don't trust the code and AI tool rights.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=120)** They are not built to reproduce accurate results, they are built to complete your prompt and they have no understanding of your project or the code you've already written or the code they output.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=132)** This means you are responsible for reviewing the code these systems generate and you can't trust them to write correct code, even if the code works.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=142)** In other words, when you work with an AI coding tool, you go from being a code writer to being a code reviewer, and you have to do extra due diligence in that job because these AI systems are very good at writing code that looks great, but may not be that great in practice.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=161)** Keep in mind, as you do so that if you provide bad examples or the wrong documentation, the AI will write code in accordance with those bad examples and wrong documentation because it has no knowledge or understanding.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=173)** Which brings us to the third and final point.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=176)** AI coding tools and the language models they're built on are deeply conservative in the sense they are biased towards old, prevalent and well-established patterns over newer ones.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=188)** In coding, they quite literally preserve the past, and this is already a challenge today and will be become a greater challenge moving forward because the predominant code on the web will always be old and established ways of doing things.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=202)** And if AI written code repeats those old patterns, they become even more predominant in newer models.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=209)** So as you work with AI coding tools, always remember they are biased towards the past and will rarely surface new modern patterns unless explicitly told to do so.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=220)** So when using these tools, it's your responsibility to stay up to date on the latest advances in the coding languages, application frameworks, and best practices for whatever you are doing.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=232)** And a big part of your job with AI is to coax and guide and sometimes force the system to resist the patterns of the past and instead use newer and more modern patterns you provide.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=245)** From my experience, AI coding tools become truly useful when you stop treating them like intelligent machines and instead start using them as tools that do quick and dirty work you need to refine.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=257)** When I use them, I provide blunt and direct instructions, question every line of code they write, throw in lots of external contextual documentation and examples, and do copious testing throughout to ensure the system doesn't start veering off the path before going totally off the rails.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=275)** When you use power tools, you use protective gear, like glasses and earplugs and gloves.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/knowledge-trust-and-conservative-models?u=76281980&t=280)** When using powerful AI tools, your protective gear is your knowledge and reasoning and contextual understanding, so use them.

#### Use AI to build the layout
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The scaffolding is already in place thanks to AI, and now I want to add some style and content to my app.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=7)** I want a header across the top, I want three equal width boxes underneath, one with information, one with an interactive map, and one with a chat.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=16)** So let's see if we can get AI to do that.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=18)** But first, I want to ensure (indistinct).
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=21)** So let's see if we can get Cursor to help us do that.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=23)** But first, I want to ensure Cursor is following my set of instructions.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=29)** For this, you can create a file called dot cursor rules, and provide system instructions for Cursor to operate on your particular project, and you place that cursor rules file inside the root of your folder, and Cursor will then always refer to it anytime it's doing something in your project.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=47)** If you want to see examples of these Cursor rules, you can go to cursor dot directory.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=52)** Here, open source contributors are creating these Cursor rules, and posting them for anyone to use.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=57)** And to use them, all you have to do is find one you like, copy the content, go into Cursor, go to the root of your project, create a new file called dot cursor rules, and just paste in the content.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=74)** Cursor is configured to automatically detect this file, and then use it as the system instruction for any future chats.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/use-ai-to-build-the-layout?u=76281980&t=81)** So whatever is in this file now governs how Cursor will write your code, and this will allow you to closely moderate how the AI is writing code to deal with all the issues we've been talking about so far in this course.

#### AI-driven code iteration
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The AI made quick work of the interactive map and the OpenAI Assistants API in this chat.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=6)** Now let's see if we can push it even further.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=9)** What I want to happen here is when the user inputs a street address in the chat, a function called is fired in the API that sends back an address.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=19)** That address is passed onto the interactive map that navigates to that address and puts a pin at the location.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=26)** And then the interactive map sends further information about the address, including the geolocation, to the Information card over here.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=34)** So for this to work, we first need to capture the function call in the OpenAI API response.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=40)** Then get the Chat box to interact with the Interactive Map box, and then get the Interactive Map box to interact with the Info box.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=49)** There's a lot going on here, and I'm interested to see how long it'll take the AI to put all of this together so it works.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=58)** For reference, I want to quickly show you the response you get in the Assistant API when you trigger a function call.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=64)** If you followed the instructions earlier in this chapter, you set up an Assistant with a function called navigateToLocation.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=71)** This function is fired anytime the user inputs an address, and it just responds with a call to navigateToLocation, which is a function that will appear in our code.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=81)** And that call has one property, address.

>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=89)** Here's what the API response looks like.
>

>

>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=176)** All right, are you ready?

>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=197)** According to my account, that took somewhere between 13 and 14 minutes.

>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=217)** Specifically, early on, there was something wrong in how the code in Chatbox was handling the function call.

> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=223)** So nothing was happening, and it took me a few tries and a few different instructions before I got the AI to write the correct code.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=231)** Now, the key to getting that to work for me is often to tell the AI to explicitly type out what's happening in the console because by making it output information in the console, it's grabbing the correct information to display in the console, and therefore, it's usually also feeding that information into the right place.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=253)** And that's one of the many tricks you'll learn as you start working with these tools yourself.

>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=286)** I also need to clean up the layout, take away this menu which has no purpose and was just added by the AI at random, and add whatever other functionality I want.

>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=310)** And you can do a lot more than what I just showed you, which is why in the text article you found earlier in this chapter, I lay out some ideas for what you can do now that the app is working properly.

>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=329)** And number two, you still need to know how to get this to work because you need to guide the AI when things start going wrong.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-driven-code-iteration?u=76281980&t=336)** And if you don't know how things work, then you're not able to provide the right instructions to the AI to get it to do what's necessary.
