#### Hallucinations, errors, and how to address them
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=0)** - If you've heard anything about AI systems, you've heard about hallucinations, this phenomenon where an AI system seems to make up facts and then present them as truth.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=10)** Now, as I've already mentioned, language models don't know anything, and don't think or reason in any way that really warrants the human metaphor language we've chosen for these computer systems.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=22)** So it follows that they also don't hallucinate.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=25)** What's actually happening is far more interesting.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=28)** This thing we call hallucinations occur when we prompt a system and it returns strings of tokens that don't replicate existing patterns within the data it was built from.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=38)** This could be because the prompt biases the system away from existing patterns mimicking the correct information, or because the prompt is requesting information there is no pattern for.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=49)** The reason the AI seems to hallucinate and be so certain about it, is language models are set up to always produce a completion, a response, even when there is no pattern that can be reproduced.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=62)** So when there is no pattern, they put together some other string of tokens that mimic what a completion of a pattern would look like.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=72)** For this in mind, for AI coding tools, a better name for hallucinations is simply errors.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=79)** When the code the AI tool outputs is wrong, it's an error, pure and simple.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=84)** If you've worked with these systems already, you know they are very good at producing these errors, and as you're working through your hands-on project, you'll encounter plenty of errors.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=94)** So, how do you deal with them?
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=97)** First of all, when you work with AI tools integrated into an IDE, you often see the errors right away because the IDE or a linting tool flags them visually, immediately.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=108)** When this happens, highlight the code, and ask the AI tool to fix it.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=113)** This often fixes the problem, but the fix may also introduce other problems.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=118)** My general approach here is to start by trying to get the system to fix just a small error, and if that doesn't work, immediately scope it out to the whole file and say there are errors online, whatever, fix them.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=133)** The AI tool will then apologize profusely, and often refactor the entire file to fix the problem.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=140)** This is an iterative approach, and you may have to go through multiple rounds to get it, right, so it's important to monitor what the AI tool does, so it doesn't take the whole project in an unhelpful direction as it's trying to fix the issue.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=155)** This is a place where the system can go really far off the rails, so use version control liberally as you do this.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=164)** Second, AI tools sometimes detect patterns and try to reproduce them even when they don't exist.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=170)** An example of this is, if you are using global JavaScript methods and asking for some new functionality, the language model may make up a new global method name following existing patterns, and then implement it in code as if that global method exists.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=188)** When you then try to run the code, the method fails because it doesn't exist, and the code crashes without explanation.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=195)** To discover this phenomenon, if you run into errors with things like global methods, the first thing to do is an internet search to see if that method exists at all.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=204)** If it does, use documentation driven development to try to resolve the issue.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=209)** If it doesn't, prompt the AI to create the new method, and it will usually produce the solution you need to move forward.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=217)** Third, and finally, because language models don't know or understand anything, if you uncritically accept every suggestion they provide, they may produce something that works, or they may produce something that only looks like it works.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=231)** This means, as you implement AI coding tools in your process, you also need to put an increased emphasis on testing your code, and for that, we already have a well-established practice, test-driven development.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/hallucinations-errors-and-how-to-address-them?u=76281980&t=245)** We'll look at this in more detail in the next chapter.

> **CLI Commands:** make (2), rails (1)
> **Definitions:** is an  (2), is a  (1)

### 4. Tests and Test-Driven Development

#### AI and the renewed importance of tests
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=0)** - Test-driven development or TDD for short is a tried and true software development methodology that is heavily used in some circles and hardly ever used in others.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=11)** With the introduction of AI coding tools, TDD has become easier and more important than ever.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=16)** And these tools also introduce some novel and interesting challenges and opportunities for how we build and test software.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=23)** So let's explore this in more detail.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=25)** Traditional test-driven development works by first writing tests to exemplify what inputs produce, what outputs, and also ensure any errors are handled correctly.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=35)** Then developing the function or component or other entity run the test on the new code to ensure it's working properly and when it does move on to the next part of the project.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=47)** With AI coding tools, each step in this process can be simplified.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=51)** The AI can hypothetically write the initial test code for you, then write the code or the function or a component or other entity, then run the test, interpret the results, and make changes.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=65)** I say, hypothetically, because at each of these steps, there is also an opportunity for the AI to get something very wrong and produce incorrect results that in turn make the project go wildly off the rails.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=78)** This may sound like a warning against using AI coding tools for TDD, and that's not at all what I'm saying.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=84)** Quite the opposite, AI coding tools are a great reminder of the importance of TDD as a practice.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=90)** And more than that, when we start relying on AI coding tools to do the practical work of writing code, robust test-driven development becomes an essential part of any project.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/ai-and-the-renewed-importance-of-tests?u=76281980&t=101)** So in this chapter, we'll take a closer look at AI-powered test-driven development.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** tdd (4)

> **Definitions:** is a  (1)
> **Warnings:** warning (1)

#### Writing tests with AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's start by doing this backwards.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=2)** I already have a React component built out, and now I need to build tests to make sure my React component is working properly.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=8)** This is something that happens to me all the time because I tend to forget to write tests as I'm building things.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=14)** And for whatever reason, my brain does not want to do test-driven development, so I often ignore it.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=20)** Now, in the past, this was a huge pain because writing tests can be really frustrating, but once you have code, it's easy to get an AI coding tool to write the tests for you.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=31)** And all you have to do is make sure those tests actually make sense to your code.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=35)** So here's how that's done using ChatGPT.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=37)** I'll start by grabbing the entire component, all its code.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=41)** Then I'll go into ChatGPT and say, "Help me write tests for this React component."
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=50)** And I'll just paste in the code.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=53)** In return, ChatGPT writes out a full set of tests for me, and this code can now be used in my project.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=60)** But before I try to implement this code in the project, I need to make sure that this test actually makes sense to what I'm doing.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=66)** So I'll go back into the chat and ask, "What conditions are you testing for?
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=75)** Explain."
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=77)** Now we'll get a natural language response that explains exactly what is going on in the tests.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=82)** This step is important because while this example is fairly easy to understand, I have two fields, a latitude and a longitude field, and the correct or incorrect parameters are very straightforward, in many cases, when you're building tests, it's far less obvious what is going on.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=101)** And it's important to make sure that the tests that are written actually tests what you are trying to do in a meaningful way.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=108)** And getting the system to explain the test like this gives you an immediate sense of what is going on in the test without having to read all the code.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=116)** We're testing for form rendering, then for validation of empty fields, then for validation of non-numeric inputs, then out of range inputs, then input scenarios, and so on.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=127)** And if you see this and you go, "There's something missing," then you can go back to the system and say, "Add this test in."
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=135)** Or if something is wrong, you can say, "That's not what I want to test for, test for this instead."
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=139)** Or you can even put in specific test scenarios and say, "I also want to test for this input and get this output."
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=146)** And this gives you the ability to guide the system to build the exact test you want.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=152)** Now, once you have a test that you like and you want to implement it into your code, you can then ask the system how to do that.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=160)** "How do I implement this into my project?"
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=167)** The chat kicks in.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=168)** It will now give you a step-by-step instruction on what to do next.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=171)** First, install the testing dependencies.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=174)** Then create the new test file.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=176)** Then set up the Jest configuration.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=179)** Then run the tests.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=181)** Then do some continuous integration if you want to.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=184)** And then verify the output.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/writing-tests-with-ai?u=76281980&t=186)** And again, if you're not happy with these instructions, just ask again and it'll give you different instructions because the system will give you a different response every time because it is a probabilistic, non-deterministic machine.

> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=187)** So it's actually passing the first set of tests, but then failing on the second one.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=191)** So here I'll say fail, copy this out, paste it into the chat, see what it says.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=199)** So it looks like we're missing something at the top here.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=202)** Let's take a look at our test code.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=206)** So here we have React, React, render, screen, testing-library, and WeatherCard.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=215)** So, oh, I think it's this one here that's the problem, so let's take that out, save, run the test again.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=224)** And this time everything passed.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=227)** So now I have a new WeatherCard component that passes my tests.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=232)** Now the one thing I didn't do that I reminded you of earlier in this chapter was to ask, "What are you testing?"
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=239)** So now that we've run the test, we have a component, everything looks to be working properly, the prudent thing to do because I have now relied entirely on the AI here and don't really know what's going on, I'll say, "What exactly are you testing in this test code?"
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=258)** Let's see.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=259)** What's it say?
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=260)** Testing for the location, temperature in Celsius, temperature in Fahrenheit, wind speed, weather icon, detailed breakdown.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=268)** Yeah, this looks reasonable.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=269)** And what you see here is using test-driven development with AI, it took me five minutes to build out a test and the component running the test, troubleshooting everything.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/effective-tdd-with-modern-ai-tools?u=76281980&t=280)** And that gives me time back to start thinking about what this component's supposed to do, how to improve it to make it better, and how to configure it in exactly the way I want to use it.

#### The challenges of AI-powered TDD
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=0)** - Now that you've seen how AI can help with test-driven development, let me highlight the main challenges you'll encounter with this approach.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=7)** First, if you're using AI coding tools to create tests either before you write your code or after the code is written, make sure the test actually tests something meaningful.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=19)** Anyone who's built an advanced application using TDD knows coming up with good tests and test cases can be a struggle.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=26)** And while AI coding tools can help with this process, they can also create meaningless tests if you're not careful.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=33)** So as you work with AI tools to build out tests, make sure they make sense, that they test meaningful parts of whatever you're building.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=43)** Otherwise, you'll end up with fancy tests that have no real purpose.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=47)** One approach I've found that works well is to write a prompt describing what the function I'm building is supposed to do, and providing a couple of examples of success states below.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=59)** Then I asked the AI tool to build out the test code and expand on my tests to include various outliers and error states one at a time.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=68)** This way, I can guide the system if it starts introducing meaningless tests and the end result is a more built out version than anything I would've generated on my own.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=80)** Second, beware of the AI building a solution for the test instead of whatever you actually need.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=88)** This is a weird one that I've encountered several times, but it's hard to replicate when you actually want to demonstrate it.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=95)** Basically, if you have a test built and then ask the AI to build a function that passes the test, the AI coding tool will sometimes either just build a function to pass the test without doing anything meaningful.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=108)** Even go as far as just pass the values through, or in extreme cases, build something that looks like the function you need and then within it, build a sub-function that passes the test without the actual function doing anything.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=122)** Usually this is relatively easy to spot and correct, but if you start relying on the AI doing its job properly, you might end up with code that passes all the tests but still doesn't work, and then you spend time figuring out what exactly is going on because your tests are no longer any help.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=140)** Like I said earlier in the course, don't trust the AI.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=144)** Always watch and check what it's doing so you can redirect it when it starts going off the path.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=151)** And finally, remember the purpose of test-driven development.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=155)** When TDD is done right, it makes software development easier and prevents accidental problems from occurring.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=162)** My go-to example for this is always name fields.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=166)** When creating a name input, it's vital to remember people's names come in all shapes and sizes and not all names use the same sets of symbols.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=175)** My name for example, often gets refused by online forms either because it's too long or because I have a hyphen in my last name or something else.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=185)** I have friends whose names include the Scandinavian letters Å, Ä, and Ö that are not supported by most name fields.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=191)** I know people whose first or last names are two or even one letter long.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=196)** There are people whose names are identical to standard software expressions like null, and there are a myriad of other edge cases that must be accounted for.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/the-challenges-of-ai-powered-tdd?u=76281980&t=207)** Building comprehensive tests for all sorts of names ensures the name field function you add to your project doesn't accidentally insist someone's name is not correct, and AI can help make that happen if you use it carefully.

### 5. Pushing Forward with Conservative Tools

#### Understanding bias in LLMs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=0)** - Language models and other AI systems are bias amplification tools.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=4)** In an oversimplified way, they are built to do pattern recognition on enormous amounts of data and then implement it to output prevalent patterns in a probabilistic way based on configuration settings like temperature and top P and a seed number.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=20)** When we prompt language models, we bias the output in the direction of our prompts.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=25)** This explains why simple zero-shot prompts give generic and often not very useful answers, while providing examples through few-shot prompts gives far more useful ones.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=37)** The examples bias the language model in the direction we want it to go.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=42)** This is a vital insight when you start working with AI coding tools because once you realize how the bias works, you can work with it to get better results.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=53)** In this chapter, we'll take a closer look at a few key strategies for guiding these conservative bias amplification machines to make them more progressive and helpful in working with modern coding standards.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=65)** As we get started, I have a few generic tips for you.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=69)** First, encoding long chats can cause bad results, in particular if the chat involves a lot of troubleshooting or iteration over code.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=79)** The reason is simple.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=80)** When you're going back and forth with a language model, the entire history of the current chat is fed back into the model as context at every new prompt.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=90)** If that chat history contains bad examples and errors, the output is biased towards those errors and the quality of the output gets worse over time.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=101)** To deal with this issue within an existing chat, I grab a best example and comprehensive context and paste it back into the chat to bring focus back on the important stuff, and I know this works because the language model will emphasize whatever's latest in the chat.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=119)** If that doesn't work, I start a brand new chat with the current example to get a clean slate.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=125)** Second, some applications like Cursor allow you to specify the context you want to work in.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=131)** This is super useful and also means if you forget to add the right context, things go off the rails almost immediately.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=138)** In other words, context is key, whether you're in a standalone chat app or in an integrated environment.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=146)** Bottom line, always check your context.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=149)** And third, if you're going to experiment with something that you know might not work or falls outside the scope of your project, do it in a separate chat.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=157)** When I'm working in a project in GitHub, Copilot, or in Cursor, and I come across a weird problem or have an idea I want to test, I bring that problem over into ChatGPT immediately.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=169)** That way the chat is independent of the project and does not clutter up the AI context memory.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/understanding-bias-in-llms?u=76281980&t=175)** Then, if I get a solution I think I can use, I'll bring it back into context in the IDE and engage the AI tool without adding noise.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** make (1), rails (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1), in other words (1)
> **Code Keywords:** super (1)
> **Env Vars:** ide (1)
> **Tools:** github (1)
> **Speakers:** - language (1)

#### Detecting amplified old patterns
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Detecting when the AI's bias is pointing towards and amplifying older standards of code requires you to have a really strong understanding of what is the modern standard for whatever coding language and application framework you are using.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=16)** That said, you can usually spot at least the most egregious examples of the AI amplifying older patterns by comparing the code the AI is outputting with, for example, the boilerplate code that comes from the application framework you're using.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=30)** One very obvious example of this is anytime you ask an AI tool to generate a React component, it always starts with import React from React.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=40)** Now this is not necessary.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=42)** This is an old standard and it's actually a really old standard and there are very few cases where you need to do this, so you can safely remove it from your code and nothing will happen.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=52)** But because it was an established standard for a very long time, it is so established that all the AI tools surface it even when it's not necessary.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=63)** So when you see this, it's a good reminder that the AI tools are already leaning on older standards.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=70)** Now previously in the course, I mentioned that this convention down here, what were calling in React function component is also an old standard and it's relatively easy to fix.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=81)** You can simply highlight the code and tell the AI, don't use this, and then it'll rewrite the code and it'll still work perfectly fine, but this isn't incorrect.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=91)** It will run just fine.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=93)** And you also notice there's no linting tool saying this is deprecated.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=97)** So that means you need to know that this is an old way of doing things.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=101)** How do you do that?
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=103)** Well, let me give you a different example.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=105)** If we go into this file here that I generated earlier and scroll down, you'll see over here it's calling in JSX dot element.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=115)** Now, when I looked through this file after the AI generated, I immediately locked in on this part here because I haven't seen this in any recent code.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=125)** And it got me thinking, is this really something we do anymore?
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=129)** And that should be your clue right there.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=132)** If something looks unfamiliar, especially in the setup of something, you should always check.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=138)** And the way you do that is you copy it out and you go onto the internet.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=142)** The easiest thing to do is just to type it in to a search bar on, for example, Google and see what it says.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=147)** And the very first suggestion you get is JSX element deprecated.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=152)** That in itself is a strong indicator that maybe this isn't something you use anymore.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=157)** And if you go and look at the search here, you'll quickly realize that that piece, JSX element, has since been replaced by React React element.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=171)** There are lots of articles and forum posts and other things that explain this, but the actual strongest indicator is if you go to the React type script library or if you go to the React documentation, you won't find reference to it.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=185)** That is usually where I go first.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=187)** So as you're working in your own project, anytime you see something that looks off from the examples that are provided by the framework, by the language or anything else, yourself, immediately go outside of your project and look it up in the documentation to see is this the current standard?
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=204)** Is this this what we should be doing?
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=206)** Or is this the AI amplifying an old pattern?
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=209)** More often than not, it's the latter.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=211)** And when that's the case, you need to update the code.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/detecting-amplified-old-patterns?u=76281980&t=214)** Otherwise you contribute to perpetuating older ways of doing things.

>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/leveraging-pattern-matching-to-push-forward?u=76281980&t=200)** And this actually steps beyond things that the AI, quote unquote, knows.

> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/leveraging-pattern-matching-to-push-forward?u=76281980&t=204)** If you start enforcing a standard the AI has no knowledge of and you do it consistently, it'll detect that standard in your other files and then repeat it in the next files you create.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/leveraging-pattern-matching-to-push-forward?u=76281980&t=215)** So you are actively guiding and preferencing and biasing the system towards your own code.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/leveraging-pattern-matching-to-push-forward?u=76281980&t=223)** But that also means when you start a new project, you have to do that process again, otherwise AI will just revert back to creating old style code.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/leveraging-pattern-matching-to-push-forward?u=76281980&t=233)** So this is an ongoing process that you have to go through every time.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/leveraging-pattern-matching-to-push-forward?u=76281980&t=238)** And the basic answer to the question, how do I do that, is you need to build yourself some very robust, modern boiler plates to start with that automatically bias the system in directions you want to go.

>

### 6. Conclusion

#### Upskilling is the new skill
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=0)** - Okay.
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=1)** While AI coding tools are enormously powerful and can be a huge help when used carefully, their usefulness and utility is entirely dependent on two things.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=10)** Authoritative sources with comprehensive documentation and code example, and a skilled and knowledgeable human developer to oversee the quality of the work and make sure the project is meeting its goals.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=22)** In other words, the core elements of good software development remain the same even as the tools change and evolve.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=29)** As you start working with AI coding tools, invest the time.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=32)** These tools save you by building and expanding your knowledge and expertise.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=37)** Read documentation, follow the development of new standards, and familiarize yourself with cutting edge tools, frameworks, and best practices.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=46)** Your job now is to push the AI coding tools to use modern practices not represented in the data they were built on.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=54)** And that can only happen if you know what those modern practices are and how they work.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=60)** With AI in our toolkit, authoritative sources and documentation become more important than ever, and you, the human developer, overseeing the work of the AI becomes the pivot point for the success of your project.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=75)** I firmly believe that AI coding tools can give developers more capabilities and more agency if we choose to use them this way.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=83)** And I firmly believe we developers can leverage the power of AI coding tools to build better software for everyone and better tools for future developers.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=92)** It all starts with embracing AI tools for what they are tools.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=98)** Now, all that's left for me to say is look it in.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/build-with-ai-beyond-pair-programming-with-ai/upskilling-is-the-new-skill?u=76281980&t=100)** Go explore ways of making AI coding tools part of your practice, and I'll see you in the next course.
